text:
I make this all the time, and it's unbelievably good!  I use this recipe exactly, except I've never tried it with garlic.  I'm going to try it next time! Also, instead of tossing the asparagus with the parmesan, I toss with all the other ingredients and lay in a single layer, then sprinkle the parmesan all over the top.  I bake mine at 350 degrees for 10-12 minutes, depending on the thickness of the asparagus.  Oh, and a hint: if you line the baking sheet with aluminum foil, there's hardly any clean up!

text:
Be sure to follow the footnote tip to remove tough part of stem by snapping the asparagus in two.  The fresher it is, the better this works, so I do this as soon as I get home from the store (also makes weeknight cooking quicker & easier when I am ready to make).  I also like to line the baking sheet with aluminum foil for easy clean up.  Instead of tossing with olive oil I spray with cooking spray after the asparagus is spread in an even layer on the sheet.  I promise it tastes just as good.  Then I sprinkle with coarse salt & fine pepper (sprinkle from up high to more evenly distribute the seasonings).

text:
I made this along with another asparagus dish (asparagus with junk from this site) because I wasn't sure which way our guests would like the asparagus. I followed the recipe except I cut down the sea salt in half, I think if you use regular table salt you can use as much as stated in the original recipe but sea salt gives it a way better flavor. I also only had parmesan & Romano cheese blend in fridge. I cleaned the asparagus drizzled with olive oil in a bowl then added the rest of the ingredients after I put the asparagus onto a cookie sheet lined with tin foil. I rolled the asparagus in salt, pepper and garlic then sprinkled the parm and roasted in oven at 325 for about 18 min. This was a huge hit, every spear was devoured. Thank You for sharing

text:
This is the ONLY way I will prepare asparagus now - it is absolutely delicious!  I don't measure out the ingredients, I just eyeball it (I don't think I get anywhere near a teaspoon of sea salt - I just sprinkle it over the asparagus after it's on the baking sheet).  12 minutes is the sweet spot in my oven for the average, grocery store bought (maybe 1/4" wide?) stalks I've used so far.  Oh, and I use shredded parmesan, not the grated stuff that comes in a can - it makes these delicious little parmesan crisps from the bits that fall onto the pan :)
Try cutting up the asparagus & throwing it into an omelet the next day - YUM!!

Very tasty recipe and definitely husband approved.  I did not use the optional ingredients only the oil, a small amount of salt and the pepper.  I did not use a separate bowl just put the asparagus on the baking tray and coated with the oil and salt and pepper.  I did not have thin asparagus so I used a trick that I saw on a cooking show and peeled the asparagus stalks. (after snapping off the woody part of the stalks.)  This was the most tender asparagus that we have even eaten.  I also baked for 10 minutes at 350 degrees since I had the main course cooking at that temp and it turned out perfect.

I actually like the taste of asparagus.  I made the recipe as written here, but discovered that I don't care for pepper or garlic or parmesan cheese on my asparagus.  I'd also recommend using vegetable oil vs. olive oil.  At this high temperature, the olive oil will impart it's flavor, and maybe overpower the asparagus flavor.   However, I am grateful for the time (12 mins) and temperature (425 degrees) because the spears came out nicely done but still firm!

Hubby and I actually scraped the pan clean, and he asked if I could figure out a way to bottle the sauce - only half-jokingly! It'll be a good addition to the rotation when asparagus is in season.

text:
Here's a fun tip for asparagus.

While snapping the asparagus is certainly the fastest and easiest way, you can also use a potato peeler to shave away some of the bottom rather than throwing it all away. The woody part is on the outside, the interior is still soft and delicious.

By peeling the ends rather than breaking them you can get almost double the amount of deliciousness, if you're willing to do a little bit of work

text:
I love roasted asparagus and the addition of lemon at the end really brightened up the flavors.  There are several problems with this recipe though in my opinion.   Cooking thin asparagus at 425 degrees for 12-15 minutes would result in mushy asparagus.  I cooked mine for 7 minutes and it was a little less than crisp tender.  I probably could have taken it out at 6 minutes.   I also think 1 tsp of salt was a little too much for our taste.  I reduced mine to between 1/4 - 1/2 tsp. and i was plenty for us.

text:
I love this recipe and make it often.  I do not believe you need the full three tablespoons of olive oil.  I use about a Tablespoon and put it in a gallon ziploc bag.  I add asparagus and toss to evenly coat.  I then take out and put on cookie sheet.  I do think you need all the salt, but it important to see that sea salt is is large flakes and that is what makes up a teaspoon of salt.  You can use regular salt, but need to cut in half.  I make with and without the garlic and everyone loves.  Good low calorie vegetable side.

text:
This was "OUT OF THIS WORLD" GOOD!  I read some reviews and then I watched the video.  I like watching those!  LOL

I went right by the recipe.  The only thing I did a little different was, I just put all the asparagus in a big zip lock bag and then added the other ingredients (except the lemon juice).  I shook the bag up real good and then baked it.  Since I'm one of those people who like those brown edges and getting something just a little done, I baked this for 20 minutes.  I did stir it around every 10 minutes or so.  The result was a wonderful, light browning of the cheese and the garlic!  IT WAS INCREDIBLE!  After I took it out of the oven, I squirted some lemon juice on it.  I like using a real lemon.  What a wonderful topper, too!  I will definitely be making this again!  It was the BEST asparagus recipe I have ever had, in my life!  I highly recommend this.  I'd give it 10 stars, if I could.  :-) A big thank you, to Swedishmilk, for sharing this recipe.  I see why it has a 5 star rating!!!!

text:
Great way to cook asparagus. The thicker asparagus is generally tenderer and better flavored, and I prefer to peel it before cooking- should develop browned patches when done- I use a 500 degree oven.  I would skip the garlic and cheese- the dish doesn't need them, they won't stick well and will burn.

text:
Loved this. Such an easy way to prepare asparagus! I followed the advice of another reviewer and lined my pan with tinfoil for easier cleanup.  I also skipped the step of mixing everything in a separate bowl.  I just sprayed the tinfoil-lined pan with cooking spray, spread out the asparagus on the pan, drizzled it with olive oil, sea salt (to taste... definitely did not use a whole teaspoon), cracked black pepper and parmesan cheese.  I tossed it together until it was well-coated right on the pan, then spread them out into a single layer.  I had really thin spears (my favorite!) and they were done in about 8 minutes at 425 in my oven.  I skipped the garlic and lemon juice this time (just plain ol forgot) but will definitely use them next time!

text:
I got some asparagus that turned out to be quite bitter, so I came here looking for something to take away the bitterness - this works!  I had some shredded Parmesan on hand, so I added the cheese on top instead of mixing it with the salt & pepper.

I lined the baking pan with foil; the asparagus stuck to it a little (possibly because I used shredded instead of the drier, grated form). Next time I'll use No Stick foil.

I like my asparagus very young and slender; 12 minutes was a bit too long. Next time I'll start checking it at 8 minutes.

This was delicious!  I did make a few changes: I used canola oil instead of olive oil and baked at 375 F to avoid smoking. I used 3 cloves of minced garlic, and eyeballed the salt and pepper. I mixed the salt, pepper, garlic, lemon, and oil in a bowl then tossed the asparagus to coat evenly. I only baked for about 10-12 minutes until the spears were soft. This side was fantastic! Will definitely be making again!

text:
What I Did:  
I didn't really measure, though amounts of oil and cheese were pretty close to that listed.  I didn't add lemon juice, and used powdered garlic instead of fresh.  

I lightly sprinkled garlic, a few pinches of kosher salt, and generous coarse ground pepper over the oiled spears, then mixed again with the cheese.

Since today's spears were the smallest I've ever bought, I took them out at 10 minutes. 

My Comments on This Recipe:
Thank you for posting this. It helped me in a pinch (I just didn't want plain steamed nor bacon-wrapped again)!  

This was a good solid recipe, that I will use again, likely increasing the cheese next time and adding it last as recommended by other reviewers.

I can't tell you how ridiculously simple this 5 star dish is to make. I didn't make many changes except that break my asparagus close to the top so that there is very little tough stem to deal with.

Also, I nix the fresh garlic for garlic salt and omit the sea salt. I combine 2 steps in 1 and it turns out great! I use fresh ground pepper from my pepper mill and omit the lemon juice. It simply doesn't need it.

You won't find a better recipe out there. This one is the ONE to use always!

None
text:
The photo is not of 'thin' asparagus. Good thing; thin asparagus are the 'male' of this bisexual plant species and are tougher if not picked fresh and prone to desiccate if overcooked. Thick female stalks will retain their superior tenderness even if they are not cut fresh and are more forgiving with regard to overcooking. I substituted melted butter for the olive oil and made sure the pan was coated nicely with a basting brush. I added a few slices of Vidalia on top of the asparagus. I removed a roast to rest from an oven at 300 F and put in the two pans of asparagus raising the temperature to 425 F. I checked through the oven glass at 12 minutes and opened the oven at 15 minutes to test their doneness, added 3 more minutes. I drizzled the juice a whole lemon over two bunches in two pans and let it sizzle with the butter. Perfection. No parmesan needed.

text:
This is an amazingly tasty recipe for asparagus.  When asparagus is in season and inexpensive, I make this a couple of times a week.  I do a couple of things different:  Instead of adding the parmesan in the mixing bowl, I sprinkle it on top just before going in the oven.  I also use a roasting rack covered in foil.  I don't ever add the lemon juice... and I adjust the bake time to match the temperature of whatever else I've got in the oven.

Also, one of my favorite restaurants has an asparagus dish that is topped with a fried egg.  I highly recommend trying that with this recipe.

text:
Delicious!! I made this for Easter and it was a big hit.  Based on the reviews I cut back on the olive oil and was glad I did. I also cut back on salt. Remember the parmesan will be salty.  I mixed the oil with the seasonings, but not the parmesan. I put the asparagus in a ziploc bag and then poured in the oil mixture in the bag. I rolled the asparagus around until it was evenly spread. I sprinkled  parmesan on one batch, but forgot to use it on the other,  so I just added it on after taking it out of the oven. Great recipe. Will be making many times in the future.

text:
Delicious!  This is my third time preparing this dish; however, I had to simplify because I hate washing greasy dishes.  After washing and drying well the asparagus.  I laid them out on parchment on a cooking tray, sprayed them with some cooking spray, lightly sprinkled some salt and pepper (no measuring) due to the salt in the cheese, then sprinkled with triple the cheese (about 1/3 cup).  Because I'm not a fan of crisp-tender vegetables, I baked for 15 minutes, lightly covered with some foil on top, and baked another 8 minutes.  Came out perfect for my taste and clean-up was a snap.

text:
I've made this around a dozen times because it has become our favorite asparagus recipe. I hate to dirty a bowl so I lay the trimmed asparagus on a foil lined cookie sheet, drizzle a little oil across and then toss them around a bit on the pan. Then I spread them out in a single layer and sprinkle with salt, pepper and a heaping teaspoon of minced garlic. I use a micro-plainer to finely shred parmesan cheese before putting them in the oven to bake at 375 for 10-15 minutes, depending on the thickness of the asparagus. Sometimes I drizzle a little lemon juice when they come out of the oven, but sometimes I forget... either way, it turns out delicious.

text:
This recipe was fantastic But I did change 2 things. I didn't add any salt because the Parmesan cheese is salty enough. I also used a lot less oil, I would say maybe 1 tablespoon would be enough.

 I didn't want to dirty a bowl and a pan so I mixed and baked the veggies in the glass baking dish.  I didn't measure anything either. I sprayed some Pam on the baking dish,  added the asparagus, the pepper and the minced garlic. I lightly drizzled the oil then gave it a good mix to coat everything! You don't need the extra  oil pooled at the bottom of the dish!

It was so easy roasting them in the oven, I definitely will make it this way from now on. I set the oven to 425F and my timer to 10 minutes, 12 minutes tops! We like a little bite to our asparagus also, as it sits for a couple minutes they still cook through a little more. Just before serving squeeze a touch of fresh lemon over the dish. 

My usual way to cook asparagus is in a skillet and I use the same ingredients. It's just as good but I have to watch and stir it more. That's why roasting is so much better. I'm sure if it's too hot outside, you would probably elect to cook them on the stovetop. Grilling them with these ingredients tastes fabulous too!

If you haven't had oven roasted asparagus, you have to give it a try. I know you'll get hooked too! By the way, I ended up eating all of them. It was the best dinner I've had in a long time! Lol
If you don't care for the ingredients suggested on the recipe, at least the te

Easy and delicious. I prefer thicker stalks for this recipe, but if using thin ones, reduce the cooking time by several minutes. Unless you enjoy very salty foods, you may want to reduce the amount of salt by as much as half. I use the optional ingredients, except for the lemon juice. If you don't have any grated parmesan, it will still be fine, but by all means, add the garlic. Don't forget to line the pan with aluminum foil or parchment paper to make cleanup a cinch.

My children automatically protest eating anything unfamiliar. Asparagus had not even been presented before it was being balked at. The word itself is not terribly appetizing, admittedly. However, honoring our usual agreement, after the first child braved it and raved, the others soon fell in line. Now all three picky eaters claim asparagus as their favorite vegetable. I agree with the shorter cook time for extra crunch. Also, I recommend that you soak it in cold water for a really crisp and fresh finished product. I skip the lemon juice and use balsamic vinaigrette instead. I've also skipped both with great results. Go for it with this recipe, it's a definite show stopper!

This is a great recipe for roasted asparagus, but a little too salty for me. I reduced the salt to 1/2 tsp. And for all those of you who reduced the temperature to 350, that is called baked asparagus. Bleh. A true roasting temperature is 400 degrees or more, which caramelizes the asparagus. Try it again at the correct temperature. It will be much better!

text:
Just made this for the first time tonight. 
This is a great dish to make for beginner's like myself. 

I agree with other commenters on here that there is way too much salt. I followed the recipe (though I forgot the lemon - next time!) and the salt was the dominant flavor by far. Fortunately we could still taste the other flavors and it's easy to tell that with less salt, this is a great recipe.  So, as others said - use about 1/3 or even 1/4 of the salt in the recipe and you should be fine. I'll definitely be making this again :).

userID:
12956362
Display Name:
mlizon
isPro:
False
followersCount:
1

madeRecipesCount:
77
favoritesCount:
208

photo:
https://images.media-allrecipes.com/userphotos/50x50/5674134.jpg
city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
Very flavorful, but way too salty as is. Easy and fast. This is my version of the recipe:

Ingredients
-1 bunch thin asparagus spears, trimmed
-3 tablespoons olive oil (or just cover them with olive oil cooking spray)
-1 & 1/2 tablespoons grated Parmesan cheese 
-1/8 tsp garlic powder 
-1/4 to 1/2 teaspoon ground black pepper
-1/2  tablespoon lemon juice 

Directions
Preheat an oven to 425 degrees F. Wash the asparagus then pat them dry with a towel, cover them in olive oil, and then place them in a large ziplock bag. In a small bowl, combine the parmesan, garlic powder and pepper. Sprinkle the mixture into the bag, then sprinkle the lemon juice in the bag as well. Shake the bag until the asparagus is coated evenly. Arrange the asparagus onto a cookie sheet in a single layer (put tin foil on the cookie sheet first for easy clean up). 
Bake in the preheated oven until just tender, 8-10 minutes depending on thickness. 8 minutes for thinner asparagus.
Review:
Rating:

This asparagus was a hit at Easter dinner! My 13 month old didn't each much else. :) I covered my cookie sheets with aluminum foil before lining up the asparagus. Just before putting them into the 350 degree preheated oven, I sprayed them liberally with cooking spray, and sprinkled with salt, pepper, and a little bit of garlic powder. They were in the oven for 10 minutes, and then I sprinkled them with parmesan and a little lemon juice. Tasty! Thank you for the recipe and the cook's note about removing the woody ends--what a huge difference! Thank you.

Made this tonight to go with the Baked Salmon II recipe on this site. I took the olive oil, put it on a plate and just took my hands and rubbed the asparagus with it. I then placed the spears on aluminium foil on a cookie sheet where I then sprinkled on the pepper, and instead of garlic and sea salt I used garlic salt, about a half teaspoon. I used fresh grated parmesan cheese and sprinkled it all over then rubbed it all together to ensure all the asparagus was coated. As I'm typing this I just realized I forgot to use the lemon at the end!! Baked at 425 for about 10 minutes and it came out pretty darn good! I'll make this again with the baked salmon.

I buy asparagus for two reasons. My husband LOVES it and my kids need to eat it - (it's nutritious and it's always important to expose your kids to different veggies!). I however, have NEVER liked asparagus... until now! Wow. I used all of the optional ingredients. VERY GOOD, this would have easily been a 5 star from my husband because anything with asparagus is 5 stars to my husband. I see more asparagus in the future for us!

Just made this recipe today for lunch and it was very good. However, the baking time is too long. I stopped at ten minutes and the asparagus was a tad overdone. (the spears I used were young and VERY thin) I would have preferred them a little crispy. And there is too much pepper in the recipe even though I love pepper. I would make this again but perhaps substitute Italian dressing for the oil/garlic/salt/lemon and bake for only 8 minutes.
